                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> A man <hi rend="ital">who has drunk a morningdraught,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">what is termed a</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">صَبُوح</foreign>; (TA;) or <hi rend="ital">who has done so, and satisfied his thirst thereby:</hi> (Aboo-'Adnán, TA:) [in the S and K it is implied that it is syn. with <foreign lang="ar">مُصْطَبِحٌ</foreign>, q. v.:] fem. <foreign lang="ar">صَبْحَى</foreign>. (S, TA.) Hence the prov., <foreign lang="ar">أَكْذَبُ مِنَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الأَخِيذِ الصَّبْحَانِ</foreign> (Aboo-'Adnán, S, TA) <hi rend="ital">More lying than the captive who had satisfied his thirst with a morning-draught:</hi> (Aboo-'Adnán, TA:) the person thus alluded to was a man who was among a people that gave him a morning-draught, after which he arose and quitted them, and was taken by another people, who said to him, “ Guide us to the place where thou wast; ” to which he replied, “ I have passed the night in the bare desert: ” but presently he sat down to make water, so they knew that he had passed the night with a people near by; and by his means they found their way to them, and exterminated them: (IAar, TA:) or the prov. is <foreign lang="ar">أَكْذَبُ مِنَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الأَخِدِ الصَّبْحَانِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">More lying than the young unweaned camel that has satisfied its thirst with drinking</hi> [<hi rend="ital">its mother's milk in the morning</hi>]; which [seems to be thirsty but] will not drink of its mother's milk when one desires it to do so: (IAar, Sh, TA:) or, accord. to Fr, <hi rend="ital">than the young unweaned camel that is affected with indigestion,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">heaviness of the stomach, from drinking much milk,</hi> and therefore craves for milk again. (Meyd. [See also Freytag's Arab. Prov.: he seems to have followed a faulty text.])          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  Also the fem., <foreign lang="ar">صَبْحَى</foreign>, A she-camel <hi rend="ital">that has been milked</hi> [app. <hi rend="ital">in the morning</hi>].       <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n23641-3" target="مَصْبَحٌ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n23655"/></foreign>, (see this last word,)] i. e. <hi rend="ital">Morning,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">forenoon, counted from sunrise to noon:</hi> (Msb and TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">مسو</foreign>:) or, accord. to some, <hi rend="ital">from midnight to noon:</hi> (TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">مسو</foreign>:) or, accord. to the Arabs, <hi rend="ital">from the beginning of the latter half of the night to the time when the sun declines from the meridian;</hi> then commences the <foreign lang="ar">مَسَآء</foreign>, extending to the end of the former half of the night; thus expl. by Th; so says El-Jawá- leekee. (Msb.) The Arabs say, when they regard a man, &amp;c., as ominous of evil, <foreign lang="ar">صَبَاحُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ٱللّٰهِ لَا صَبَاحُكَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">God's morning: not thy morning</hi>]: and if you will, you may say, <foreign lang="ar">صَبَاحَ ٱللّٰهِ لَا صَبَاحَكَ</foreign>. (Lh, TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">عِمْ صَبَاحًا</foreign>, (S,) or <foreign lang="ar">عِمُوا صَبَاحًا</foreign>, (K,) lit. imperative, but meaning a prayer, i. e. <hi rend="ital">May thy life,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">your life, be pleasant during the morning,</hi> (Har p. 32, and TA * in arts. <foreign lang="ar">نعم</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">وعم</foreign>,) is a salutation of the people of the Time of Ignorance. (TA.) One says also, <foreign lang="ar">لَقِيتُهُ صَبَاحًا</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">ذَا صَبَاحٍ</foreign>, (S,) or <foreign lang="ar">أَتَيْتُهُ ذَا صَبَاحٍ</foreign>, (K,) which [i. e. <foreign lang="ar">ذا صباح</foreign>] is only used adverbially, (Sb, S, K,) except in the dial. of Khath'am, (Sb, S,) meaning [<hi rend="ital">I met him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">I came to him,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">in a morning,</hi> [or] <hi rend="ital">between daybreak and sunrise:</hi> (K:) the following verse (S, TA) by Anas Ibn-Nuheyk, of Khath'am, (TA,) or, as some say, by Iyás Ibn-Mudrikeh El-Hanafee, (so in a marg. note in a copy of the S,) presents an exception to the adverbial usage: <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">عَزَمْتُ عَلَى إِقَامَةِ ذِى صَبَاحٍ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">لِأَمْرٍ مَّا يُسَوَّدُ مَنْ يَسُودُ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> (S, TA:) the poet means, <hi rend="ital">I determined to stay until the time of the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">صباح</foreign> [i. e. either <hi rend="ital">dawn</hi> or <hi rend="ital">forenoon</hi>]: for <hi rend="ital">it is on account of some particular thing,</hi> i. e. some good quality, or some praiseworthy thing, <hi rend="ital">that he is made a chief who becomes a chief:</hi> thus Ibn-Es-Seeráfee explains this verse. (TA.) And one says,   
      <foreign lang="ar">أَتَيْتُهُ ذَا <ref cref="n23641-4" target="صَبُوحٍ" n="4" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, not used otherwise than adverbially, meaning the same as <foreign lang="ar">ذَا صَبَاحٍ</foreign>, expl. above; (K;) and   
      <foreign lang="ar">ذَاتَ <ref cref="n23641-5" target="الصَّبُوحِ" n="5" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">in the morning,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">first part of day, before sunrise:</hi> (IAar, TA:) or   
      <foreign lang="ar">ذَا <ref cref="n23641-6" target="صَبُوحٍ" n="6" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> [properly means] <hi rend="ital">in a time of drinking the</hi> [<hi rend="ital">morning-draught called</hi>] <foreign lang="ar">صَبُوح</foreign>. (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">أَتَيْتُهُ <ref cref="n23641-7" target="صَبِيحَةَ" n="7" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>يَوْمِ كَذَا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I came to him in the dawn,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">in the morning,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">forenoon, of such a day</hi>]: (A:) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n23641-8" target="أُصْبُوحَةَ" n="8" lang="ar" type="7" subtype="WOTF"/> كُلِّ يَوْمٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">in the morning of every day</hi>]; and in like manner, <foreign lang="ar">أُمْسِيَّةَ كُلِّ يَوْمٍ</foreign>. (S.) And <foreign lang="ar">أَتَيْتُهُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">صَبَاحَ مَسَآءَ</foreign>, (Sb, A, TA,) for <foreign lang="ar">صَبَاحًا وَمَسَآءً</foreign>, [<hi rend="ital">I came to him morning</hi> and <hi rend="ital">evening,</hi>] meaning <hi rend="ital">every morning and evening:</hi> (Sharh esh-Shudhoor, p. 31:) the two nouns are thus constructed by some of the Arabs, after the manner of <foreign lang="ar">خَمْسَةَ عَشَرَ</foreign>: but some prefix the former noun to the other, putting the latter in the gen. case, except when the expression is used as a denotative of state, or adverbially: (TA:) [or, accord. to IHsh,] <foreign lang="ar">صَبَاحَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مَسَآءٍ</foreign> is allowable as [an adverbial expression] meaning <foreign lang="ar">صَبَاحَ ذَا مَسَآءٍ</foreign> [lit. <hi rend="ital">in a morning having an evening,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">in a forenoon having an afternoon</hi>]; and a similar instance occurs in the Kur, ch. lxxix. last verse. (Sharh esh-Shudhoor, ubi suprà.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">يَوْمُ الصَّبَاحِ</foreign> means <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">The day of the hostile,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">predatory, incursion.</hi> (S, A, K.) The Arabs, when suddenly attacked in the morning by a troop of horsemen, cry aloud, <foreign lang="ar">يَا صَبَاحَاهْ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">O! a hostile,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">predatory, incursion!</hi>]; warning the whole tribe: (TA:) this is said by him who calls for aid: (JM:) for they generally made a hostile, or predatory, incursion in the morning: (TA, JM:) or, as some say, the two conflicting parties used, when night came, to abstain; and when day returned, they recommenced; so that the case is as though he who said thus meant, The time of the <foreign lang="ar">صَبَاح</foreign> [or morning] has come, therefore prepare yourselves for fighting.
